Santos </font></div><div style="padding-left:194.4pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">McGuireWoods LLP </font></div><div id="i80db026aa4914920b3be47ea6a7a0a94_111"></div><div style="text-align:center"><font><br></font></div><div style="text-align:center"><font><br></font></div><div style="text-align:center"><font><br></font></div><div style="text-align:center"><font><br></font></div><div style="text-align:center"><font><br></font></div><div style="text-align:center"><font><br></font></div><div style="text-align:center"><font><br></font></div><div style="text-align:center"><font><br></font></div><div style="text-align:center"><font><br></font></div><div style="height:72pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div style="text-align:center"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">13</font></div><div><font><br></font></div></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><div style="min-height:72pt;width:100%"><div><font><br></font></div></div><div style="text-align:center"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:700;line-height:232%">ATTACHMENT A-1</font></div><div style="text-align:center"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:700;line-height:125%;text-decoration:underline">FACTUAL BASIS FOR BREACH</font></div><div style="text-align:center"><font><br></font></div><div style="text-align:justify;text-indent:36pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">1.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%;padding-left:27pt">The United States&#8217; Factual Basis for the Breach of the January 7, 2021 Deferred Prosecution Agreement (the &#8220;DPA&#8221;), which DPA was between the United States Department of Justice, Criminal Division, Fraud Section (the &#8220;Fraud Section&#8221;) and the United States Attorney&#8217;s Office for the Northern District of Texas (the &#8220;USAO-NDTX&#8221;) (collectively, the &#8220;Offices&#8221;), and the Defendant, The Boeing Company (&#8220;Defendant,&#8221; &#8220;Boeing,&#8221; or the &#8220;Company&#8221;) is incorporated by reference as part of the non-prosecution agreement, dated May 29, 2025, between the Offices and Boeing. The parties stipulate that the representations and views herein belong to the Offices.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:4pt;margin-top:18pt;padding-left:36pt;text-indent:-18pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:700;line-height:125%;text-decoration:underline">I.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:700;line-height:125%;padding-left:10.34pt;text-decoration:underline">Background and Relevant DPA Obligations</font></div><div style="text-align:justify;text-indent:36pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">2.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%;padding-left:27pt">On January 7, 2021, the United States filed a one-count criminal Information (the &#8220;Information&#8221;) in the United States District Court for the Northern District of Texas, charging Boeing with one count of conspiracy to defraud the United States, in violation of Title 18, United States Code, Section 371, that is, knowingly and willfully, and with the intent to defraud, conspired and agreed together with others to defraud the United States by impairing, obstructing, defeating, and interfering with, by dishonest means, the lawful function of a United States government agency, to wit, the Federal Aviation Administration Aircraft Evaluation Group (&#8220;FAA AEG&#8221;) within the United States Department of Transportation, in connection with the FAA AEG&#8217;s evaluation of the Boeing 737 MAX airplane&#8217;s Maneuvering Characteristics Augmentation System, including for purposes of the 737 MAX Flight Standardization Board Report and the 737 MAX differences-training determination.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Aptos',san-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%"> </font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">See</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%"> </font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">United States v. The Boeing Company</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">, 21-cr-00005-O (ECF No. 1).</font></div><div style="height:72pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div style="text-align:center"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">A-1-1</font></div></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><div style="min-height:72pt;width:100%"><div><font><br></font></div></div><div style="text-align:justify;text-indent:36pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">3.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%;padding-left:27pt">The same day, the United States also filed the DPA between the United States and Boeing. </font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">See </font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">ECF No. 4. In exchange for Boeing agreeing, among other things, &#8220;to implement a compliance and ethics program designed, implemented, and enforced to prevent and detect violations of the U.S. fraud laws throughout its operations,&#8221; the United States agreed to defer prosecution of Boeing for the conduct set forth in the Statement of Facts attached to the DPA, including the conspiracy charged in the Information, for the three-year term of the DPA. </font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">Id</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">. &#182;&#182; 21, 22, 24. The United States further agreed that, if Boeing complied fully with the terms of the DPA, the United States would move to dismiss the Information described in Paragraph 1 of the DPA six months after the term of the DPA expired. </font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">Id</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">. &#182; 25. The DPA provided, however, that if the United States determined during the six-month period following the end of the term of the DPA that Boeing had breached the DPA during the DPA term, the United States could pursue remedies for the breach, including by prosecuting the Company for any federal criminal violation of which the Offices have knowledge, including, but not limited to, the charges in the Information. </font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">Id</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">. &#182;&#182; 25&#8211;26. As part of the DPA, the Company also agreed, among other things, to pay a criminal monetary penalty of $243,600,000, an Airline Compensation Amount of $1,770,000,000, and a Crash-Victim Beneficiaries Compensation Amount of $500,000,000 to the heirs, relatives, and&#47;or legal beneficiaries of the crash victims of Lion Air Flight 610 and Ethiopian Airlines Flight 302.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:400;line-height:232%"> Id</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">. &#182;&#182; 10, 12, 13.</font></div><div style="height:72pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div style="text-align:center"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">A-1-2</font></div></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><div style="min-height:72pt;width:100%"><div><font><br></font></div></div><div style="text-align:justify;text-indent:36pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">4.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%;padding-left:27pt">Relevant to the United States&#8217; breach determination, Paragraphs 21 and 22 of the DPA state&#58;</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:12pt;padding-left:72pt;padding-right:72pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">21. &#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;The Company represents that it has implemented and will continue to implement a compliance and ethics program designed, implemented, and enforced to prevent and detect violations of the U.S. fraud laws throughout its operations, including those of its subsidiaries, affiliates, agents, and joint ventures, and those of its contractors and subcontractors whose responsibilities relate to the Company&#8217;s interactions with any domestic or foreign government agency (including the FAA), regulator, or any of its airline customers, including, but not limited to, the minimum elements set forth in Attachment C.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:12pt;padding-left:72pt;padding-right:72pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">22. &#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;In order to address any deficiencies in its internal controls, policies, and procedures, the Company represents that it has undertaken, and will continue to undertake in the future, in a manner consistent with all of its obligations under this Agreement, a review of its existing internal controls, policies, and procedures regarding compliance with U.S. fraud laws, focusing on the Company&#8217;s interactions with domestic or foreign government agencies (including the FAA), regulators, and any of its airline customers. Where necessary and appropriate, the Company agrees to adopt a new compliance program, or to modify its existing one, including internal controls, compliance policies, and procedures in order to ensure that it maintains an effective compliance program, including a system of internal controls, designed to effectively detect and deter violations of U.S. fraud laws. The compliance program, including the internal controls system, will include, but not be limited to, the minimum elements set forth in Attachment C &#91;which outlined the requirements for the Company&#8217;s compliance program&#93;.</font></div><div style="height:72pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div style="text-align:center"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">A-1-3</font></div></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><div style="min-height:72pt;width:100%"><div><font><br></font></div></div><div style="margin-bottom:12pt;padding-left:36pt;text-indent:-18pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:700;line-height:125%">II.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:700;line-height:125%;padding-left:5.68pt;text-decoration:underline">The United States&#8217; Breach Determination</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:125%;text-decoration:underline"> </font></div><div style="text-align:justify;text-indent:36pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">5.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%;padding-left:27pt">At the time of the conduct described in Attachment A-2, Boeing did not have a centralized compliance function. Boeing appointed its first Global Chief Compliance Officer (&#8220;CCO&#8221;) and established its Global Compliance function (&#8220;Global Compliance&#8221; or &#8220;Compliance&#8221;) in May of 2020. During the term of the DPA, Boeing took considerable steps to enhance the independence, capability, and effectiveness of its compliance program. Among other things, Boeing enhanced its annual Compliance Risk Management process, including in ways that strengthened compliance controls with respect to potential safety and quality risks, and took steps to integrate compliance efforts across its business. As direct remediation of the charged misconduct, Boeing implemented policies and procedures to manage and coordinate the formal communication of information between Boeing and its regulators and customers and mandatory training regarding transparency in interactions with regulators and customers. Despite these enhancements, in the Offices&#8217; view, Boeing failed to sufficiently extend its anti-fraud ethics and compliance program over its quality and manufacturing process before the end of the DPA term. As a result, the Department determined that Boeing&#8217;s anti-fraud compliance program still has significant gaps.</font></div><div style="text-align:justify;text-indent:36pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">6.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%;padding-left:27pt">The United States, in an exercise of the discretion conferred upon it by the agreed upon terms of the DPA (namely, Paragraph 26 of the DPA), has determined that Boeing violated Paragraphs 21 and 22 and Attachment C of the DPA and declared a breach of the DPA on May 14, 2024. Relevant considerations in arriving at that determination and making that declaration include the following&#58;</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:8pt;padding-left:72pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:-18pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:125%">&#8226;</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:125%;padding-left:13.8pt">Boeing failed to fully satisfy the requirement to &#8220;create and foster a culture of ethics and compliance with the law in its day-to-day operations,&#8221; Attachment C &#182; 1, by failing to mitigate known manufacturing and quality risks&#59;</font></div><div style="height:72pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div style="text-align:center"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">A-1-4</font></div></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><div style="min-height:72pt;width:100%"><div><font><br></font></div></div><div style="margin-bottom:8pt;padding-left:72pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:-18pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:125%">&#8226;</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:125%;padding-left:13.8pt">Boeing failed to fully satisfy the requirement to implement &#8220;compliance policies and procedures designed to reduce the prospect of violations of U.S. fraud laws and the Company&#8217;s compliance code,&#8221; Attachment C &#182; 3, by failing to design a compliance and ethics program that included sufficient anti-fraud oversight of Boeing&#8217;s quality and safety processes&#59;</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:8pt;padding-left:72pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:-18pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:125%">&#8226;</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:125%;padding-left:13.8pt">Boeing failed to fully satisfy the requirement to implement &#8220;compliance policies and procedures designed to reduce the prospect of violations of U.S. fraud laws and the Company&#8217;s compliance code,&#8221; Attachment C &#182; 3, by failing to implement sufficient controls concerning the risk that Boeing&#8217;s airworthiness certifications to the FAA could be incomplete, inaccurate, false and&#47;or fraudulent&#59; </font></div><div style="margin-bottom:8pt;padding-left:72pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:-18pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:125%">&#8226;</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:125%;padding-left:13.8pt">Boeing failed to fully satisfy the requirement to implement &#8220;compliance policies and procedures designed to reduce the prospect of violations of U.S. fraud laws and the Company&#8217;s compliance code,&#8221; Attachment C &#182; 3, by failing to implement sufficient controls concerning the risk of incomplete, inaccurate, false and&#47;or fraudulent statements in Boeing&#8217;s manufacturing records&#59; and </font></div><div style="margin-bottom:8pt;padding-left:72pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:-18pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:125%">&#8226;</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:125%;padding-left:13.8pt">Boeing failed to fully satisfy the requirement to appropriately develop and adjust &#8220;compliance policies and procedures on the basis of a periodic risk assessment addressing the individual circumstances of the Company,&#8221; Attachment C &#182; 4, and to review and update such policies &#8220;as appropriate to ensure their continued effectiveness,&#8221; Attachment C &#182; 5, in light of known manufacturing and quality risks, and the attendant risks of incomplete, inaccurate, false, and&#47;or fraudulent statements to the FAA.</font></div><div style="height:72pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div style="text-align:center"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">A-1-5</font></div></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><div style="min-height:72pt;width:100%"><div><font><br></font></div></div><div style="margin-bottom:12pt;padding-left:36pt;text-indent:-18pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:700;line-height:125%">III.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:700;line-height:125%;padding-left:1.02pt;text-decoration:underline">Failure to Extend Anti-Fraud Compliance Program Over Quality and Manufacturing Processes </font></div><div style="margin-bottom:12pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:36pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">7.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%;padding-left:27pt">Before delivering a 737 MAX aircraft to a U.S. customer, Boeing must apply to the FAA for a U.S. Airworthiness Certificate for each aircraft. In so doing, Boeing certifies to the FAA &#8220;that the aircraft has been inspected and is airworthy,&#8221; meaning, &#8220;the aircraft conforms to its type design and is in a condition for safe operation.&#8221; FAA Form 8130-6&#59; 14 C.F.R. &#167; 3.5. A Boeing employee makes this certification in reliance on the completeness, accuracy, and truthfulness of the Company&#8217;s build records and the effectiveness of related manufacturing and quality processes. Although Boeing knew about manufacturing, quality, safety, and anti-fraud risks capable of undermining the completeness, accuracy, and truthfulness of those records, Boeing did not implement additional or sufficient controls concerning the risk that its certifications of airworthiness to the FAA could be incomplete, inaccurate, false and&#47;or fraudulent and that aircraft delivered to its customers &#8220;conforms to its type design and is in a condition for safe operation.&#8221; The Department has determined that these failures breached the DPA, as set forth above and below. </font></div><div style="margin-bottom:12pt;padding-left:72pt;text-indent:-36pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:700;line-height:125%">A.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:700;line-height:125%;padding-left:24.34pt">Out-of-Sequence Work </font></div><div style="text-align:justify;text-indent:36pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">8.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%;padding-left:27pt">Boeing&#8217;s instructions for aircraft assembly require assembly to occur in a particular sequence. When a sequenced step is performed inadequately or not completed, it may be discovered and corrected at a later stage. Correction of the inadequate or incomplete work must then be done &#8220;out-of-sequence.&#8221; Out-of-sequence work is more difficult to perform, increases the risk that defects in manufacturing will occur, and may require installed parts to be removed and later re-installed.</font></div><div style="height:72pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div style="text-align:center"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">A-1-6</font></div></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><div style="min-height:72pt;width:100%"><div><font><br></font></div></div><div style="text-align:justify;text-indent:36pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">9.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%;padding-left:27pt">Between 2021 and 2023, Boeing conducted several Safety Risk Management assessments that identified out-of-sequence work as a risk factor that could cause the delivery of an &#8220;unairworthy&#8221; or non-conforming aircraft to Boeing&#8217;s customers. Despite the acknowledgement of this risk, the Safety Risk Management assessments did not sufficiently consider measures to reduce out-of-sequence work. Boeing senior executives prioritized the movement of aircraft through Boeing&#8217;s factories over reducing out-of-sequence work to ensure production quality. Boeing did not implement sufficient policies or procedures to mitigate the risk posed by out-of-sequence work. </font></div><div style="text-align:justify;text-indent:36pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">10.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%;padding-left:21pt">Moreover, although fraud is an inherent risk in production and quality compliance activities, Boeing&#8217;s Safety Risk Management assessments also failed to identify out-of-sequence risk as a fraud risk or consider enhanced production procedures, or preventive or detective controls, to mitigate the risk. Boeing&#8217;s Global Compliance function, which is responsible for Boeing&#8217;s anti-fraud ethics and compliance program, was not involved in the Safety Risk Assessments. Compliance therefore did not evaluate fraud risks associated with out-of-sequence work, including the risk of incomplete, inaccurate, false, and&#47;or fraudulent statements to the FAA. </font></div><div style="margin-bottom:12pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:36pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">11.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%;padding-left:21pt">The United States has determined that Boeing&#8217;s failure to identify and adjust its ethics and compliance program to address the anti-fraud risks attendant to out-of-sequence work violated its obligation to meet the compliance program standards required by DPA Attachment C, including Paragraphs 1, 4, and 5. </font></div><div style="height:72pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div style="text-align:center"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">A-1-7</font></div></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><div style="min-height:72pt;width:100%"><div><font><br></font></div></div><div style="margin-bottom:12pt;padding-left:72pt;text-indent:-36pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:700;line-height:125%">B.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:700;line-height:125%;padding-left:25pt">Completeness of Records </font></div><div style="text-align:justify;text-indent:36pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">12.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%;padding-left:21pt">Boeing&#8217;s airworthiness certifications to the FAA rely on the completeness and accuracy of Boeing&#8217;s build records and the effectiveness of related manufacturing and quality processes. If installed parts are later removed during manufacturing, Boeing policy requires Boeing employees to document the removal in certain written records. The creation of a removal record initiates a process to ensure proper reinstallation of the part and record the individuals involved in removal, reinstallation, and reinspection. If a removal record was not completely resolved in Boeing&#8217;s computer systems, including reinstallation and reinspection, a Boeing employee would not certify an aircraft as airworthy to the FAA. </font></div><div style="text-align:justify;text-indent:36pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">13.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%;padding-left:21pt">A failure to create a removal record prevents Boeing from verifying that parts are correctly or completely re-installed and that its certification stating that the plane is &#8220;airworthy&#8221; is accurate. This recordkeeping failure could also undermine Boeing&#8217;s processes for effectively responding to, investigating, and remediating potential allegations of violations of the U.S. fraud laws or the Company&#8217;s compliance code, policies, and procedures, in part because Boeing could lack records of who was involved in removing, reinstalling, and reinspecting disturbed installations and what they did. </font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">See </font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">DPA Attachment C &#182; 10. </font></div><div style="height:72pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div style="text-align:center"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">A-1-8</font></div></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><div style="min-height:72pt;width:100%"><div><font><br></font></div></div><div style="margin-bottom:12pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:36pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">14.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%;padding-left:21pt">Boeing received numerous reports of incidents of non-compliance with its policy governing removals throughout the DPA term. In addition, since 2019, the FAA has issued numerous formal or informal actions to Boeing related to Boeing&#8217;s policy governing removals. Compliance was not sufficiently involved in root cause analysis, remediation, or risk mitigation related to this process, notwithstanding the (1) impact non-compliance with Boeing&#8217;s policy governing removals could have on Boeing&#8217;s representations regarding its aircraft, and (2) recordkeeping consequences. Boeing failed to meet the compliance program standards required by DPA Attachment C, including Paragraphs 3, 4, and 5.</font></div><div style="height:72pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div style="text-align:center"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">A-1-9</font></div></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><div style="min-height:72pt;width:100%"><div><font><br></font></div></div><div style="margin-bottom:12pt;padding-left:72pt;text-indent:-36pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:700;line-height:125%">C.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:700;line-height:125%;padding-left:24.34pt">Stamping Issues in Build Records</font></div><div style="text-align:justify;text-indent:36pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">15.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%;padding-left:21pt">Throughout the build process, Boeing mechanics and inspectors affirm (or &#8220;stamp&#8221;) that they have completed work in conformance with requirements. Stamped manufacturing and quality records are important for Boeing&#8217;s certification to the FAA that an aircraft is airworthy. All build plans and required inspections must be stamped by Boeing employees as complete to requirements before a Boeing employee certifies an aircraft as airworthy to the FAA. Boeing relies on those build and quality stamping records to certify to the FAA that an aircraft is airworthy. False statements in Boeing&#8217;s build records pose a fraud risk because they could undermine the completeness, accuracy, and truthfulness of Boeing&#8217;s representations and certifications to the FAA regarding its aircraft, among other issues. Boeing received hundreds of reports of stamping non-compliance through its internal reporting channels. Boeing Compliance identified this anti-fraud risk during the DPA term and issued training and communications throughout the Company in response to the risk. Despite awareness of stamping non-compliance reports, Boeing did not conduct sufficient testing to evaluate whether its stamping integrity communications and training efforts were effective in practice and stamping issues persisted.</font></div><div style="height:72pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div style="text-align:center"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">A-1-10</font></div></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><div style="min-height:72pt;width:100%"><div><font><br></font></div></div><div style="text-align:justify;text-indent:36pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">16.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%;padding-left:21pt">In or around April 2024, Boeing disclosed to the Fraud Section false stamping during the DPA term at the Boeing 787 manufacturing facility in Charleston, South Carolina. The false stamps caused Boeing&#8217;s quality management systems to reflect that all required steps were complete, when they were not. Employees involved in the false stamping did not understand Boeing&#8217;s stamping policy, were not familiar with its requirements, and were not effectively trained on it. Because the build and quality records are the cornerstone of Boeing&#8217;s certification that aircraft conform to their approved type design, the lack of understanding by Boeing employees of the importance of and requirements for stamping integrity calls into question the effectiveness of Boeing&#8217;s anti-fraud compliance program with respect to the certifications.  </font></div><div style="text-align:justify;text-indent:36pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">17.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%;padding-left:21pt">These reported stamping issues highlighted several shortcomings in Boeing&#8217;s anti-fraud compliance program with respect to stamping integrity, including the following weaknesses&#58; </font></div><div style="margin-bottom:8pt;padding-left:72pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:-18pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">&#8226;</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%;padding-left:13.8pt">Boeing did not effectively evaluate its stamping policy to ensure it was effective. Specifically, Boeing failed to measure employee understanding of the policy, including whether employees understood that stamping, build, and quality records were the basis for Boeing&#8217;s certification to the FAA of airworthiness. </font></div><div style="margin-bottom:8pt;padding-left:72pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:-18pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">&#8226;</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%;padding-left:13.8pt">Boeing did not effectively ensure compliance with its stamping policy. </font></div><div style="margin-bottom:8pt;padding-left:72pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:-18pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">&#8226;</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%;padding-left:13.8pt">Boeing did not implement enhanced or remedial controls to prevent or detect stamping policy violations. Rather, Boeing continued to rely on its existing build and inspection record process to support its certification to the FAA of aircraft airworthiness. </font></div><div style="height:72pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div style="text-align:center"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">A-1-11</font></div></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><div style="min-height:72pt;width:100%"><div><font><br></font></div></div><div style="text-align:justify;text-indent:36pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">18.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%;padding-left:21pt">Complete, accurate, and truthful build records are the basis for Boeing&#8217;s certification of airworthiness to the FAA. In the face of known manufacturing, quality, safety, and anti-fraud risks which undermine the completeness, accuracy, and truthfulness of those records, Boeing failed to implement additional or sufficient controls concerning the risk that certifications of airworthiness to the FAA could be incomplete, inaccurate, false and&#47;or fraudulent and that aircraft delivered to its customers &#8220;conform&#91;&#93; to its type design and is in a condition for safe operation,&#8221; in violation of the compliance program standards required by DPA Attachment C, including Paragraphs 3, 4, and 5.</font></div><div id="i80db026aa4914920b3be47ea6a7a0a94_133"></div><div style="padding-left:2.9pt;padding-right:2.9pt;text-align:center"><font><br></font></div><div style="height:72pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div style="text-align:center"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">A-1-12</font></div></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><div style="min-height:72pt;width:100%"><div><font><br></font></div></div><div style="padding-left:2.9pt;padding-right:2.9pt;text-align:center"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:700;line-height:232%">ATTACHMENT A-2</font></div><div style="padding-left:2.9pt;padding-right:2.9pt;text-align:center"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:700;line-height:232%;text-decoration:underline">STATEMENT OF FACTS</font></div><div offense&#58;</font></div><div style="padding-left:5.4pt;padding-right:5.4pt;text-align:center"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New style="min-height:72pt;width:100%"><div><font><br></font></div></div><div style="padding-left:36pt;padding-right:5.75pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:-18pt"><font Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%;padding-left:9.08pt">The Boeing 737 was a commercial airplane that could seat approximately 200 passengers and was one of Boeing&#8217;s best-selling airplane models.</font><font style="color:#231f20;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;letter-spacing:0.166em;line-height:232%"> </font><font style="color:#231f20;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">Boeing began designing, manufacturing, and selling the Boeing 737 in the 1960s.</font><font style="color:#231f20;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;letter-spacing:0.166em;line-height:232%"> </font><font style="color:#231f20;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">Over time, Boeing designed, manufactured, and sold new versions of the Boeing 737 to its rivals in commercial airplanes, Company-1.</font><font style="color:#231f20;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;letter-spacing:0.166em;line-height:232%"> </font><font style="color:#231f20;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">Like the new version of Company-1&#8217;s airplane, the 737 MAX promised APPROVAL</font></div><div style="padding-left:36pt"><font><br></font></div><div style="padding-left:36pt"><font><br></font></div><div style="text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;WHEREAS, The Boeing Company (the &#8220;Company&#8221;) has been engaged in discussions with the United States Department of Justice, Criminal Division, Fraud Section and the United States Attorney&#8217;s Office for the Northern District of Texas (collectively, the &#8220;Offices&#8221;) regarding issues arising in relation to the Offices&#8217; investigation of violation of U.S. fraud laws by certain of the Company&#8217;s employees&#59; </font></div><div style="text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;WHEREAS, on January 7, 2021 in the U.S. District Court for the Northern District of Texas, 4&#58;21-cr-00005-O, the Offices filed a one-count Information (the &#8220;Information&#8221;) charging the Company with one count of Conspiracy to Defraud the United States, in violation of Title 18, United States Code, Section 371&#59; </font></div><div style="text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;WHEREAS, on January 7, 2021, the Offices deferred prosecution of the Information pursuant to a deferred prosecution agreement (the &#8220;DPA&#8221;), 4&#58;21-cr-00005-O, Dkt. No. 4&#59;</font></div><div style="text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;WHEREAS, on May 14, 2024, the Offices determined that the Company breached the DPA&#59;</font></div><div style="text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;WHEREAS, the Company has been engaged in discussions with the Offices regarding the Offices&#8217; determination that the Company breached the DPA&#59;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</font></div><div style="text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;WHEREAS, in order to resolve such discussions, it is proposed that the Company enter into a non-prosecution agreement with the Offices (the &#8220;Agreement&#8221;) and the Offices move to dismiss the Information without prejudice, and the Company consents to the same&#59; </font></div><div style="text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;WHEREAS, the Board of Directors of the Company (the &#8220;Board&#8221;) has been extensively briefed on discussions with the Offices regarding an agreement to resolve the Offices&#8217; investigation and determination that the Company breached the DPA&#59;</font></div><div style="height:72pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div style="text-align:center"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New of the Company, together with outside counsel for the Company&#59; and such counsel have advised the Board of the Company&#8217;s rights, possible defenses, and the consequences of entering into the Agreement with the Offices and consenting to the motion to dismiss without prejudice&#59; and the Board agreed that the Company should enter into an agreement on those terms and delegated to the President and Chief Executive Officer, the Chief Legal Officer, and other management the authority to finalize and execute the Agreement consistent with the principal terms briefed to the Board and subject to the final approval of the Chair of the Board&#59;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</font></div><div style="text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;WHEREAS, the Chair of the Board has reviewed documents relevant to the Agreement, and has been advised that the material terms of the final documents are consistent with the terms of the Agreement previously described to the Board&#59;</font></div><div style="text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;Therefore, the Chair of the Board of Directors to whom the Board delegated authority has provided approval as to the following&#58;</font></div><div style="padding-left:36pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:-18pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%;padding-left:9pt">The Company agrees and consents to dismissal of the Information without prejudice and agrees that the Company is not a prevailing party for purposes of the Hyde Amendment&#59;</font></div><div style="height:72pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div style="text-align:center"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">2.</font><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%;padding-left:9pt">The Company (a) enters into this non-prosecution agreement (&#8220;Agreement&#8221;) with the Offices&#59; (b) agrees to pay an overall criminal monetary penalty amount of $487,200,000, which reflects a fine at the top of the applicable Sentencing Guidelines fine range and the maximum fine allowable under Title 18, United States Code, Sections 371 and 3571(c), including credit for the $243,600,000 previously paid by the Company pursuant to the DPA, resulting in a remaining criminal penalty to be paid by the Company of $243,600,000, which will be paid to the United States Treasury, and to pay such penalty in accordance with terms set forth in the Agreement and with respect to the conduct described in the Statement of Facts in Attachment A-2&#59; (c) agrees to pay victim compensation to the heirs, relatives, and&#47;or legal beneficiaries of the crash victims of Lion Air Flight 610 and Ethiopian Airlines Flight 302 (collectively, &#8220;Crash Victim Families&#8221;) in the amount of $444.5 million&#59; (d) agrees to make a sustained monetary investment in its compliance and safety programs of at least $455,000,000 as set forth in the Agreement&#59; (e) agrees to retain an Independent Compliance Consultant to assess the Company&#8217;s progress regarding remediation and implementation of the compliance measures described in Attachment C to the Agreement, in accordance with Attachment D to the Agreement&#59; (f) agrees to ensure that its Board of Directors holds a meeting with the Crash Victim Families, should they wish to attend, and their legal representatives&#59; (g) agrees to cooperate with and report to the Offices in accordance with the Agreement&#59; and (h) agrees to continue to implement a compliance and ethics program reasonably designed, implemented, and enforced to prevent and detect violations of U.S. fraud laws throughout its operations, including, but not limited to, the minimum elements set forth in Attachment C of the Agreement. </font></div><div style="height:72pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div style="text-align:center"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%;padding-left:9pt">The Company accepts the terms and conditions of this Agreement, including, but not limited to, (a) a knowing waiver for purposes of this Agreement and any charges by the United States arising out of the conduct described in the attached Statement of Facts of any objection with respect to venue in the United States District Court for the Northern District of Texas&#59; and (b) a knowing waiver of any defenses based on the statute of limitations for any prosecution relating to the conduct described in the attached Statement of Facts or relating to conduct known to the Offices prior to the date on which the NPA was signed that is not time-barred by the applicable statute of limitations on the date of the signing of the NPA&#59;</font></div><div style="padding-left:36pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:-18pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New with the principal terms briefed to the Board of Directors, and to agree and consent to dismissal of the Information without prejudice&#59;</font></div><div style="padding-left:36pt;text-align:justify;text-indent:-18pt"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'Times New Roman',sans-serif;font-size:12pt;font-weight:400;line-height:232%">5.</font><font
